# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of github.com/sg-evals)/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — examined for [reason]
- path/to/file2.ext — examined for [reason]
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Symptom observed in: path/to/symptom.ext
2. Called from: path/to/caller.ext (function name)
3. Bug triggered by: path/to/buggy.ext (function name, line ~N)
...

## Root Cause
- **File**: path/to/root_cause.ext
- **Function**: function_name()
- **Line**: ~N
- **Explanation**: [Why this code is buggy]

## Proposed Fix
```diff
- buggy code
+ fixed code
```

## Analysis
[Detailed trace from symptom to root cause, explaining each step]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- Root cause identification: Did you find the correct file(s) where the bug originates?
- Call chain accuracy: Did you trace the correct path from symptom to root cause?
- Fix quality: Is the proposed fix correct and minimal?

67-assistanttext-
Excellent! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Kubernetes scheduler bug. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Investigation Summary

**Bug Identified:** Missing ResourceSlice event handler in the Kubernetes scheduler's event-driven re-queuing mechanism.

### Root Cause

The scheduler has **two critical missing pieces** that prevent ResourceSlice creation/update events from triggering pod re-evaluation:

1. **Missing GVK Constant** (`pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`):
   - No `ResourceSlice` constant defined in the GVK constants section
   - All other DRA resources (ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.) are defined, but ResourceSlice is missing

2. **Missing Event Handler Registration** (`pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`):
   - The `addAllEventHandlers()` function has a switch statement that registers event handlers for all tracked resources
   - No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement
   - When the scheduler starts, it never registers a handler for ResourceSlice events

### Why It's A Bug

The dynamicresources plugin:
- Reads ResourceSlices via `resourceSliceLister` during Prefilter to check available resources
- Returns "cannot allocate" when no ResourceSlices exist
- Pods get added to the unschedulable queue
- When a DRA driver later publishes ResourceSlices with available resources:
  - **Event posted to API server** ✓
  - **No scheduler handler registered** ✗ (THE BUG)
  - Event silently dropped
  - Pod never re-evaluated
  - **Pod remains stuck forever**

### The Fix

Three minimal changes (15 lines total):

1. Add `ResourceSlice GVK = "ResourceSlice"` constant
2. Add ResourceSlice case in eventhandlers.go switch statement (following exact pattern of ResourceClaim)
3. Optionally add ResourceSlice events to the dynamicresources pl
... (truncated)

Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = {\n240: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n241: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n242: \t\t\t\tPod:         pod,\n243: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n244: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap: framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: runPermitStatus},\n245: \t\t\t\t},\n246: \t\t\t}\n247: \t\t\tfitErr.Diagnosis.AddPluginStatus(runPermitStatus)\n248: \t\t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, framework.NewStatus(runPermitStatus.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n249: \t\t}\n250: \n251: \t\treturn ScheduleResult{nominatingInfo: clearNominatedNode}, assumedPodInfo, runPermitStatus\n252: \t}\n253: \n254: \t// At the end of a successful scheduling cycle, pop and move up Pods if needed.\n255: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n256: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n257: \t\t// Clear the entries after activation.\n258: \t\tpodsToActivate.Map = make(map[string]*v1.Pod)\n259: \t}\n260: \n261: \treturn scheduleResult, assumedPodInfo, nil\n262: }\n263: \n264: // bindingCycle tries to bind an assumed Pod.\n265: func (sched *Scheduler) bindingCycle(\n266: \tctx context.Context,\n267: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n268: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n269: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n270: \tassumedPodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n271: \tstart time.Time,\n272: \tpodsToActivate *framework.PodsToActivate) *framework.Status {\n273: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n274: \n275: \tassumedPod := assumedPodInfo.Pod\n276: \n277: \t// Run \"permit\" plugins.\n278: \tif status := fwk.WaitOnPermit(ctx, assumedPod); !status.IsSuccess() {\n279: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n280: \t\t\tfitErr := &framework.FitError{\n281: \t\t\t\tNumAllNodes: 1,\n282: \t\t\t\tPod:         assumedPodInfo.Pod,\n283: \t\t\t\tDiagnosis: framework.Diagnosis{\n284: \t\t\t\t\tNodeToStatusMap:      framework.NodeToStatusMap{scheduleResult.SuggestedHost: status},\n285: \t\t\t\t\tUnschedulablePlugins: sets.New(status.Plugin()),\n286: \t\t\t\t},\n287: \t\t\t}\n288: \t\t\treturn framework.NewStatus(status.Code()).WithError(fitErr)\n289: \t\t}\n290: \t\treturn \t}\n302: \n303: \t// Calculating nodeResourceString can be heavy. Avoid it if klog verbosity is below 2.\n304: \tlogger.V(2).Info(\"Successfully bound pod to node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(assumedPod), \"node\", scheduleResult.SuggestedHost, \"evaluatedNodes\", scheduleResult.EvaluatedNodes, \"feasibleNodes\", scheduleResult.FeasibleNodes)\n305: \tmetrics.PodScheduled(fwk.ProfileName(), metrics.SinceInSeconds(start))\n306: \tmetrics.PodSchedulingAttempts.Observe(float64(assumedPodInfo.Attempts))\n307: \tif assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp != nil {\n308: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n309: \t\tmetrics.PodSchedulingSLIDuration.WithLabelValues(getAttemptsLabel(assumedPodInfo)).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(*assumedPodInfo.InitialAttemptTimestamp))\n310: \t}\n311: \t// Run \"postbind\" plugins.\n312: \tfwk.RunPostBindPlugins(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n313: \n314: \t// At the end of a successful binding cycle, move up Pods if needed.\n315: \tif len(podsToActivate.Map) != 0 {\n316: \t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.Activate(logger, podsToActivate.Map)\n317: \t\t// Unlike the logic in schedulingCycle(), we don't bother deleting the entries\n318: \t\t// as `podsToActivate.Map` is no longer consumed.\n319: \t}\n320: \n321: \treturn nil\n322: }\n323: \n324: func (sched *Scheduler) handleBindingCycleError(\n325: \tctx context.Context,\n326: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n327: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n328: \tpodInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo,\n329: \tstart time.Time,\n330: \tscheduleResult ScheduleResult,\n331: \tstatus *framework.Status) {\n332: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n333: \n334: \tassumedPod := podInfo.Pod\n335: \t// trigger un-reserve plugins to clean up state associated with the reserved Pod\n336: \tfwk.RunReservePluginsUnreserve(ctx, state, assumedPod, scheduleResult.SuggestedHost)\n337: \tif forgetErr := sched.Cache.ForgetPod(logger, assumedPod); forgetErr != nil {\n338: \t\tlogger.Error(forgetErr, \"scheduler cache ForgetPod failed\")\n339: \t} else {\n340: \t\t// \"Forget\"ing an assumed Pod in binding cycle should be treated as a PodDelete event,\n341: \t\t// as the assumed Pod had occupied a certain amount of resources in scheduler cache.\n342: \t\t//\n343: \t\t// Avoid moving the assumed Pod itself as it's always Unschedulable.\n344: \t\t// It's intentional to \"defer\" this operation; otherwise MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue() would\n345: \t\t// add this event to in-flight events and thus move the assumed pod to backoffQ anyways if the plugins don't have appropriate QueueingHint.\n346: \t\tif status.IsRejected() {\n347: \t\t\tdefer sched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, func(pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n348: \t\t\t\treturn assumedPod.UID != pod.UID\n349: \t\t\t})\n350: \t\t} else {\n351: \t\t\tsched.SchedulingQueue.MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue(logger, internalqueue.AssignedPodDelete, assumedPod, nil, nil)\n352: \t\t}\n353: \t}\n354: \n355: \tsched.FailureHandler(ctx, fwk, podInfo, status, clearNominatedNode, start)\n356: }\n357: \n358: func (sched *Scheduler) frameworkForPod(pod *v1.Pod) (framework.Framework, error) {\n359: \tfwk, ok := sched.Profiles[pod.Spec.SchedulerName]\n360: \tif !ok {\n361: \t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"profile not found for scheduler name %q\", pod.Spec.SchedulerName)\n362: \t}\n363: \treturn fwk, nil\n364: }\n365: \n366: // skipPodSchedule returns true if we could skip scheduling the pod for specified cases.\n367: func (sched *Scheduler) skipPodSchedule(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, pod *v1.Pod) bool {\n368: \t// Case 1: pod is being deleted.\n369: \tif pod.DeletionTimestamp != nil {\n370: \t\tfwk.EventRecorder().Eventf(pod, nil, v1.EventTypeWarning, \"FailedScheduling\", \"Scheduling\", \"skip schedule deleting pod: %v/%v\", pod.Namespace, pod.Name)\n371: node list.\n388: // If it succeeds, it will return the name of the node.\n389: // If it fails, it will return a FitError with reasons.\n390: func (sched *Scheduler) schedulePod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) (result ScheduleResult, err error) {\n391: \ttrace := utiltrace.New(\"Scheduling\", utiltrace.Field{Key: \"namespace\", Value: pod.Namespace}, utiltrace.Field{Key: \"name\", Value: pod.Name})\n392: \tdefer trace.LogIfLong(100 * time.Millisecond)\n393: \tif err := sched.Cache.UpdateSnapshot(klog.FromContext(ctx), sched.nodeInfoSnapshot); err != nil {\n394: \t\treturn result, err\n395: \t}\n396: \ttrace.Step(\"Snapshotting scheduler cache and node infos done\")\n397: \n398: \tif &framework.FitError{\n410: \t\t\tPod:         pod,\n411: \t\t\tNumAllNodes: sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NumNodes(),\n412: \t\t\tDiagnosis:   diagnosis,\n413: \t\t}\n414: \t}\n415: \n416: \t// When only one \t\tFeasibleNodes:  len(feasibleNodes),\n437: \t}, err\n438: }\n439: \n440: // Filters the nodes to find the ones that fit the pod based on the framework\n441: // filter plugins and filter extenders.\n442: func (sched *Scheduler) findNodesThatFitPod(ctx context.Context, fwk framework.Framework, state *framework.CycleState, pod *v1.Pod) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, framework.Diagnosis, error) {\n443: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n444: \tdiagnosis := framework.Diagnosis{\n445: \t\tNodeToStatusMap: make(framework.NodeToStatusMap),\n446: \t}\n447: \n448: \tallNodes, err := sched.nodeInfoSnapshot.NodeInfos().List()\n449: \tif err != nil {\n450: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n451: \t}\n452: \t// Run \"prefilter\" plugins.\n453: \tpreRes, s := fwk.RunPreFilterPlugins(ctx, state, pod)\n454: \tif !s.IsSuccess() {\n455: \t\tif !s.IsRejected() {\n456: \t\t\treturn nil, diagnosis, s.AsError()\n457: \t\t}\n458: \t\t// All nodes in NodeToStatusMap will have the same status so that they can be handled in the preemption.\n459: \t\t// Some non trivial refactoring is needed to avoid this copy.\n460: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n461: \t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = s\n462: \t\t}\n463: \n464: \t\t// Record the messages from PreFilter in Diagnosis.PreFilterMsg.\n465: \t\tmsg := s.Message()\n466: \t\tdiagnosis.PreFilterMsg = msg\n467: \t\tlogger.V(5).Info(\"Status after running PreFilter plugins for pod\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"status\", msg)\n468: \t\tdiagnosis.AddPluginStatus(s)\n469: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, nil\n470: \t}\n471: \n472: \t// \"NominatedNodeName\" can potentially be set in a previous scheduling cycle as a result of preemption.\n473: \t// This node is likely the only candidate that will fit the pod, and hence we try it first before iterating over all nodes.\n474: \tif len(pod.Status.NominatedNodeName) > 0 {\n475: \t\tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.evaluateNominatedNode(ctx, pod, fwk, state, diagnosis)\n476: \t\tif err != nil {\n477: \t\t\tlogger.Error(err, \"Evaluation failed on nominated node\", \"pod\", klog.KObj(pod), \"node\", pod.Status.NominatedNodeName)\n478: \t\t}\n479: \t\t// Nominated node passes all the filters, scheduler is good to assign this node to the pod.\n480: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) != 0 {\n481: \t\t\treturn feasibleNodes, diagnosis, nil\n482: \t\t}\n483: \t}\n484: \n485: \tnodes := allNodes\n486: \tif !preRes.AllNodes() {\n487: \t\tnodes = make([]*framework.NodeInfo, 0, len(preRes.NodeNames))\n488: \t\tfor _, n := range allNodes {\n489: \t\t\tif !preRes.NodeNames.Has(n.Node().Name) {\n490: \t\t\t\t// We consider Nodes that are filtered out by PreFilterResult as rejected via UnschedulableAndUnresolvable.\n491: \t\t\t\t// We have to record them in NodeToStatusMap so that they won't be considered as candidates in the preemption.\n492: \t\t\t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[n.Node().Name] = framework.NewStatus(framework.UnschedulableAndUnresolvable, \"node is filtered out by the prefilter result\")\n493: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n494: \t\t\t}\n495: \t\t\tnodes = append(nodes, n)\n496: \t\t}\n497: \t}\n498: \tfeasibleNodes, err := sched.findNodesThatPassFilters(ctx, fwk, state, pod, &diagnosis, nodes)\n499: \t// always try to update the sched.nextStartNodeIndex regardless of whether an error has occurred\n500: \t// this is helpful to make sure that all the nodes have a chance to be searched\n501: \tprocessedNodes := len(feasibleNodes) + len(diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n502: \tsched.nextStartNodeIndex = (sched.nextStartNodeIndex + processedNodes) % len(nodes)\n503: \tif err != nil {\n504: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n505: \t}\n506: \n507: \tfeasibleNodesAfterExtender, err := findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx, sched.Extenders, pod, feasibleNodes, diagnosis.NodeToStatusMap)\n508: \tif err != nil {\n509: \t\treturn nil, diagnosis, err\n510: \t}\n511: \tif len(feasibleNodesAfterExtender) != len(feasibleNodes) {\n512: \t\t// Extenders filtered out some nodes.\n513: \t\t//\n514: \t\t// Extender doesn't support any kind of requeueing feature like EnqueueExtensions in the scheduling framework.\n515: \t\t// When Extenders reject some Nodes and the pod ends up being unschedulable,\n516: \t\t// we put framework.ExtenderName to pInfo.UnschedulablePlugins.\n517: \t\t// This Pod will be requeued from unschedulable pod pool to activeQ/backoffQ\n518: \t\t// by any kind of cluster events.\n519: \t\t// https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/122019\n520: \t\tif diagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins == nil {\n521: \t\t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins = sets.New[string]()\n522: \t\t}\n523: \t\tdiagnosis.UnschedulablePlugins.Insert(framework.ExtenderName)\n524: \t}\n525: \n526: \treturn feasibleNodesAfterExtender, diagnosis, nil\n527: }\n528: \n529: func (sched *Scheduler) nil\n547: }\n548: \n549: // hasScoring checks if scoring nodes is configured.\n550: func (sched *Scheduler) hasScoring(fwk framework.Framework) bool {\n551: \tif fwk.HasScorePlugins() {\n552: \n562: // hasExtenderFilters checks if any extenders filter nodes.\n563: func (sched *Scheduler) hasExtenderFilters() bool {\n564: \tfor _, extender := range sched.Extenders {\n565: \t\tif *Scheduler) findNodesThatPassFilters(\n574: \tctx context.Context,\n575: \tfwk framework.Framework,\n576: \tstate *framework.CycleState,\n577: \tpod *v1.Pod,\n578: \tdiagnosis *framework.Diagnosis,\n579: \tnodes []*framework.NodeInfo) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n580: \tnumAllNodes := len(nodes)\n581: \tnumNodesToFind := sched.numFeasibleNodesToFind(fwk.PercentageOfNodesToScore(), int32(numAllNodes))\n582: \tif !sched.hasExtenderFilters() && !sched.hasScoring(fwk) {\n583: \t\tnumNodesToFind = 1\n584: \t}\n585: \n586: \t// Create feasible list with enough space to avoid growing it\n587: \t// and allow assigning.\n588: \tfeasibleNodes := make([]*framework.NodeInfo, numNodesToFind)\n589: \n590: \tif \t}\n596: \n597: \terrCh := parallelize.NewErrorChannel()\n598: \tvar feasibleNodesLen int32\n599: \tctx, cancel := context.WithCancel(ctx)\n600: \tdefer cancel()\n601: \n602: \ttype nodeStatus struct {\n603: \t\tnode   string\n604: \t\tstatus *framework.Status\n605: \t}\n606: \tresult := make([]*nodeStatus, numAllNodes)\n607: \tcheckNode := func(i int) {\n608: \t\t// We check the nodes starting from where we left off in the previous scheduling cycle,\n609: \t\t// this is to make sure all nodes have the same chance of being examined across pods.\n610: \t\tnodeInfo := length > numNodesToFind {\n619: \t\t\t\tcancel()\n620: \t\t\t\tatomic.AddInt32(&feasibleNodesLen, -1)\n621: \t\t\t} else {\n622: \t\t\t\tfeasibleNodes[length-1] = nodeInfo\n623: \t\t\t}\n624: \t\t} else {\n625: \t\t\tresult[i] = &nodeStatus{node: nodeInfo.Node().Name, status: status}\n626: \t\t}\n627: \t}\n628: \n629: \tbeginCheckNode := time.Now()\n630: \tstatusCode := framework.Success\n631: \tdefer func() {\n632: \t\t// We record Filter extension point latency here instead of in framework.go because framework.RunFilterPlugins\n633: \t\t// function is called for each node, whereas we want to have an overall latency for all nodes per scheduling cycle.\n634: \t\t// Note that this latency also includes latency for `addNominatedPods`, which calls framework.RunPreFilterAddPod.\n635: \t\tmetrics.FrameworkExtensionPointDuration.WithLabelValues(metrics.Filter, statusCode.String(), fwk.ProfileName()).Observe(metrics.SinceInSeconds(beginCheckNode))\n636: \t}()\n637: \n638: \t// Stops searching for more nodes once the configured number of feasible nodes\n639: \t// are found.\n640: \tfwk.Parallelizer().Until(ctx, numAllNodes, checkNode, metrics.Filter)\n641: \tfeasibleNodes = feasibleNodes[:feasibleNodesLen]\n642: \tfor _, item := range result {\n643: \t\tif item == nil {\n644: \t\t\tcontinue\n645: \t\t}\n646: \t\tdiagnosis.NodeToStatusMap[item.node] = item.status\n647: \treturn feasibleNodes, nil\n654: }\n655: \n656: // numFeasibleNodesToFind returns the number of feasible nodes that once found, the scheduler stops\n657: // its search for more feasible nodes.\n658: func (sched *Scheduler) numFeasibleNodesToFind(percentageOfNodesToScore *int32, numAllNodes int32) (numNodes int32) {\n659: \tif numAllNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n660: \t\treturn numAllNodes\n661: \t}\n662: \n663: \t// Use profile percentageOfNodesToScore if it's set. Otherwise, use global percentageOfNodesToScore.\n664: \tvar percentage int32\n665: \tif percentageOfNodesToScore != nil {\n666: \t\tpercentage = *percentageOfNodesToScore\n667: \t} else {\n668: \t\tpercentage = sched.percentageOfNodesToScore\n669: \t}\n670: \n671: \tif percentage == 0 {\n672: \t\tpercentage = int32(50) - numAllNodes/125\n673: \t\tif percentage < minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind {\n674: \t\t\tpercentage = minFeasibleNodesPercentageToFind\n675: \t\t}\n676: \t}\n677: \n678: \tnumNodes = numAllNodes * percentage / 100\n679: \tif numNodes < minFeasibleNodesToFind {\n680: \t\treturn minFeasibleNodesToFind\n681: \t}\n682: \n683: \treturn numNodes\n684: }\n685: \n686: func findNodesThatPassExtenders(ctx context.Context, extenders []framework.Extender, pod *v1.Pod, feasibleNodes []*framework.NodeInfo, statuses framework.NodeToStatusMap) ([]*framework.NodeInfo, error) {\n687: \tlogger := klog.FromContext(ctx)\n688: \t// Extenders are called sequentially.\n689: \t// Nodes in original feasibleNodes can be excluded in one extender, and pass on to the next\n690: \t// extender in a decreasing manner.\n691: \tfor _, extender := range extenders {\n692: \t\tif len(feasibleNodes) == 0 {\n693: \t\t\tbreak\n694: \t\t}\n695: \t\tif !extender.IsInterested(pod) {\n696: \t\t\tcontinue\n697: \t\t}\n698: \n699: \t\t// Status of failed nodes in failedAndUnresolvableMap will be added or overwritten in <statuses>,\n700: \t\t// so that the scheduler framework can respect the UnschedulableAndUnresolvable status for\n701: \t\t// particular nodes, and this may eventually improve preemption efficiency.\n702: \t\t// Note: users are recommended to configure the extenders that may return UnschedulableAndUnresolvable\n703: \t\t// status ahead of others.\n704: \t\tfeasibleList, failedMap, failedAndUnresolvableMap, err := extender.Filter(pod, feasibleNodes)\n705: \t\tif err != nil {\n706: \t\t\tif extender.IsIgnorable() {\n707: \t\t\t\tlogger.Info(\"Skipping extender as it returned error and has ignorable flag set\", \"extender\", extender, \"err\", err)\n708: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n709: \t\t\t}\n710: \t\t\treturn nil, err\n711: \t\t}\n712: \n713: \t\tfor failedNodeName, failedMsg := range failedAndUnresolvableMap {\n714: \t\t\tvar aggregatedReasons \\n859: // selectHost takes a prioritized list of nodes and then picks one\\n860: // in a reservoir sampling manner from the nodes that had the highest score.\\n861: // It also returns the top {count} Nodes,\\n862: // and the top of the list will be always the selected host.\\n863: func selectHost(nodeScoreList []framework.NodePluginScores, count int) (string, []framework.NodePluginScores, error) {\\n864: \\tif len(nodeScoreList) == 0 {\\n865: \\t\\treturn \\\"\\\", nil, errEmptyPriorityList\\n866: \\t}\\n867: \\n868: \\tvar h nodeScoreHeap = nodeScoreList\\n869: \\theap.Init(&h)\\n870: 0, count)\\n874: \\tsortedNodeScoreList = append(sortedNodeScoreList, heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores))\\n875: \\n876: \\t// This for-loop will continue until all Nodes with the highest scores get checked for a reservoir sampling,\\n877: \\t// and sortedNodeScoreList gets (count - 1) elements.\\n878: \\tfor ns := heap.Pop(&h).(framework.NodePluginScores); ; ns = \\n883: \\t\\tif ns.TotalScore == sortedNodeScoreList[0].TotalScore {\\n884: \\t\\t\\tcntOfMaxScore++\\n885: \\t\\t\\tif rand.Intn(cntOfMaxScore) == 0 {\\n886: \\t\\t\\t\\t// Replace the candidate n-1]\\n931: \\treturn x\\n932: }\\n933: \\n934: // assume signals to the cache that a pod is already in the cache, so that binding can be asynchronous.\\n935: // assume modifies `assumed`.\\n936: func {
  "content": "# Kubernetes Scheduler ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Investigation\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` \u2014 Entry point for scheduling cycle\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 Event handler registration mechanism for all cluster events\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` \u2014 GVK constants for all tracked resource types\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 DRA plugin implementation and EventsToRegister\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/resourceslice.go` \u2014 ResourceSlice informer factory\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go` \u2014 Resource model building from ResourceSlices\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` (ScheduleOne function, line 66-134)\n   - Pod scheduling occurs, fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod is added to unschedulable queue\n   - No re-evaluation happens when ResourceSlices are created\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (scheduler initialization)\n   - Calls `addAllEventHandlers()` to register event handlers for resource changes\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (addAllEventHandlers function, line 285-546)\n   - Registers event handlers for multiple resource types via a gvkMap switch statement (lines 395-543)\n   - **MISSING**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement\n   - Covers: CSINode, CSIDriver, CSIStorageCapacity, PersistentVolume, PersistentVolumeClaim, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, StorageClass\n\n4. **Framework issue in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (GVK constants, lines 68-106)\n   - **MISSING**: No `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined\n   - ResourceSlices are used by the dynamicresources plugin but not declared as a trackable event resource\n\n5. **Resource model built in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (Prefilter method, line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` which loads all ResourceSlices\n   - When a ResourceSlice is added/updated, this model should be invalidated and pods re-evaluated\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Two missing pieces that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-evaluation:**\n\n### 1. Missing GVK Constant\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Function**: Constants section\n- **Line**: Should be around line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n- **Issue**: ResourceSlice GVK constant is not defined, so the framework doesn't know about this resource type\n\n### 2. Missing Event Handler Registration\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Line**: ~448-492 (the switch statement that handles all gvk cases)\n- **Issue**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the gvkMap switch statement\n  - The switch iterates through gvkMap (which comes from plugins' EventsToRegister)\n  - When ResourceSlice is NOT in gvkMap, it never gets an event handler registered\n  - Therefore, when a ResourceSlice is created/updated, the scheduler is never notified\n\n### 3. Missing Event Declaration in Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386-411\n- **Issue**: No event for ResourceSlice Add/Update (though this is driven by the plugin's needs)\n\n## Why This Is A Bug\n\nThe dynamicresources plugin depends on ResourceSlices to determine:\n1. Which resources are available on each node\n2. How many resources are allocated/free\n3. Whether a pod can be scheduled based on resource availability\n\nWhen a ResourceSlice is created/updated:\n- The plugin reads it via `resourceSliceLister` to build the resource model\n- Pods that were previously unschedulable due to insufficient resources might now be schedulable\n- **BUT**: Without an event handler, the scheduler never knows to re-queue these pods for re-evaluation\n- Result: Pods remain stuck in Unschedulable state indefinitely\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (lines 68-96)\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n\tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\t// ...\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (lines 448-492)\n\nAdd a new case in the gvkMap switch statement in `addAllEventHandlers()`:\n\n```diff\n\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t// ... existing code ...\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice to EventsToRegister (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (lines 386-412)\n\nAdd ResourceSlice events to the EventsToRegister method:\n\n```diff\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlice information is used to check device availability on nodes.\n+\t\t// When a driver provides additional resource availability information, pods may become schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// ... rest of events ...\n\t}\n```\n\nAnd add the missing queueing hint function:\n\n```diff\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo) framework.QueueingHintFn {\n+\t// Any change to a ResourceSlice may affect resource availability.\n+\t// Pods waiting on resource availability need to be re-evaluated.\n+\treturn framework.Queue\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Flow\n\n1. **Pod Arrives Before DRA Driver**:\n   - Pod requests a DRA device via ResourceClaim\n   - Scheduler runs dynamicresources plugin's Prefilter\n   - Plugin calls `resourceSliceLister.List()` \u2192 no ResourceSlices exist yet\n   - Plugin returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" \u2192 pod goes to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlice**:\n   - Driver creates a ResourceSlice with available resources\n   - Event is posted to the API server\n   - **BUG**: Scheduler has no handler registered for ResourceSlice events\n   - Event is silently dropped (no informer callback)\n   - Unschedulable pod is never re-evaluated\n\n3. **Pod Remains Stuck**:\n   - ResourceSlice exists with available resources\n   - Pod's claim could now be allocated\n   - But scheduler never learned about the ResourceSlice update\n   - Pod stays in Pending/Unschedulable forever\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThe root cause is a missing integration between the informer system and the scheduler's event loop:\n\n1. **The Framework Contract**: When a plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares it cares about an event type (e.g., ResourceSlice), the scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` should register an informer callback for that event.\n\n2. **The Missing Link**:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT declared in the GVK constants (first bug)\n   - Therefore, it cannot be referenced in EventsToRegister\n   - Even if declared in EventsToRegister, there's no handler case for it (second bug)\n   - Result: ResourceSlice events never reach the scheduler queue\n\n3. **The Fix Is Minimal**:\n   - Add one GVK constant (1 line)\n   - Add one switch case with 6-10 lines of code\n   - Add one optional queueing hint function (3-4 lines)\n   - Total: ~15 lines of code\n\n### Impact\n\n- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod\n- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

  "originalFile": "# Kubernetes Scheduler ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Investigation\n\n## Files Examined\n- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` \u2014 Entry point for scheduling cycle\n- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 Event handler registration mechanism for all cluster events\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` \u2014 GVK constants for all tracked resource types\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 DRA plugin implementation and EventsToRegister\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/resourceslice.go` \u2014 ResourceSlice informer factory\n- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go` \u2014 Resource model building from ResourceSlices\n\n## Dependency Chain\n\n1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` (ScheduleOne function, line 66-134)\n   - Pod scheduling occurs, fails with \"cannot allocate all claims\"\n   - Pod is added to unschedulable queue\n   - No re-evaluation happens when ResourceSlices are created\n\n2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (scheduler initialization)\n   - Calls `addAllEventHandlers()` to register event handlers for resource changes\n\n3. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (addAllEventHandlers function, line 285-546)\n   - Registers event handlers for multiple resource types via a gvkMap switch statement (lines 395-543)\n   - **MISSING**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement\n   - Covers: CSINode, CSIDriver, CSIStorageCapacity, PersistentVolume, PersistentVolumeClaim, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, StorageClass\n\n4. **Framework issue in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (GVK constants, lines 68-106)\n   - **MISSING**: No `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined\n   - ResourceSlices are used by the dynamicresources plugin but not declared as a trackable event resource\n\n5. **Resource model built in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (Prefilter method, line 958)\n   - Calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` which loads all ResourceSlices\n   - When a ResourceSlice is added/updated, this model should be invalidated and pods re-evaluated\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Two missing pieces that prevent ResourceSlice events from triggering pod re-evaluation:**\n\n### 1. Missing GVK Constant\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n- **Function**: Constants section\n- **Line**: Should be around line 96 (after ResourceClassParameters)\n- **Issue**: ResourceSlice GVK constant is not defined, so the framework doesn't know about this resource type\n\n### 2. Missing Event Handler Registration\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n- **Function**: `addAllEventHandlers()`\n- **Line**: ~448-492 (the switch statement that handles all gvk cases)\n- **Issue**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the gvkMap switch statement\n  - The switch iterates through gvkMap (which comes from plugins' EventsToRegister)\n  - When ResourceSlice is NOT in gvkMap, it never gets an event handler registered\n  - Therefore, when a ResourceSlice is created/updated, the scheduler is never notified\n\n### 3. Missing Event Declaration in Plugin\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386-411\n- **Issue**: No event for ResourceSlice Add/Update (though this is driven by the plugin's needs)\n\n## Why This Is A Bug\n\nThe dynamicresources plugin depends on ResourceSlices to determine:\n1. Which resources are available on each node\n2. How many resources are allocated/free\n3. Whether a pod can be scheduled based on resource availability\n\nWhen a ResourceSlice is created/updated:\n- The plugin reads it via `resourceSliceLister` to build the resource model\n- Pods that were previously unschedulable due to insufficient resources might now be schedulable\n- **BUT**: Without an event handler, the scheduler never knows to re-queue these pods for re-evaluation\n- Result: Pods remain stuck in Unschedulable state indefinitely\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### Fix 1: Add ResourceSlice GVK Constant\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (lines 68-96)\n\n```diff\nconst (\n\t// ... existing constants ...\n\tPodSchedulingContext    GVK = \"PodSchedulingContext\"\n\tResourceClaim           GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"\n\tResourceClass           GVK = \"ResourceClass\"\n\tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n\tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n\t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n\t// ...\n)\n```\n\n### Fix 2: Add ResourceSlice Event Handler Registration\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (lines 448-492)\n\nAdd a new case in the gvkMap switch statement in `addAllEventHandlers()`:\n\n```diff\n\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n\t\t\t); err != nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn err\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n\t\t}\n+\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t}\n\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n\t\t// ... existing code ...\n```\n\n### Fix 3: Add ResourceSlice to EventsToRegister (Optional but Recommended)\n\n**File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` (lines 386-412)\n\nAdd ResourceSlice events to the EventsToRegister method:\n\n```diff\n\tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n\t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n\t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n\t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n\t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n\t\t// may be schedulable.\n\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n+\t\t// ResourceSlice information is used to check device availability on nodes.\n+\t\t// When a driver provides additional resource availability information, pods may become schedulable.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange},\n\t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n\t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n\t\t//\n\t\t// ... rest of events ...\n\t}\n```\n\nAnd add the missing queueing hint function:\n\n```diff\n+func (pl *dynamicResources) isSchedulableAfterResourceSliceChange(logger klog.Logger, podInfo *framework.QueuedPodInfo) framework.QueueingHintFn {\n+\t// Any change to a ResourceSlice may affect resource availability.\n+\t// Pods waiting on resource availability need to be re-evaluated.\n+\treturn framework.Queue\n+}\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### The Bug Flow\n\n1. **Pod Arrives Before DRA Driver**:\n   - Pod requests a DRA device via ResourceClaim\n   - Scheduler runs dynamicresources plugin's Prefilter\n   - Plugin calls `resourceSliceLister.List()` \u2192 no ResourceSlices exist yet\n   - Plugin returns \"cannot allocate all claims\" \u2192 pod goes to unschedulable queue\n\n2. **DRA Driver Starts and Creates ResourceSlice**:\n   - Driver creates a ResourceSlice with available resources\n   - Event is posted to the API server\n   - **BUG**: Scheduler has no handler registered for ResourceSlice events\n   - Event is silently dropped (no informer callback)\n   - Unschedulable pod is never re-evaluated\n\n3. **Pod Remains Stuck**:\n   - ResourceSlice exists with available resources\n   - Pod's claim could now be allocated\n   - But scheduler never learned about the ResourceSlice update\n   - Pod stays in Pending/Unschedulable forever\n\n### Why This Matters\n\nThe root cause is a missing integration between the informer system and the scheduler's event loop:\n\n1. **The Framework Contract**: When a plugin's `EventsToRegister()` declares it cares about an event type (e.g., ResourceSlice), the scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` should register an informer callback for that event.\n\n2. **The Missing Link**:\n   - ResourceSlice is NOT declared in the GVK constants (first bug)\n   - Therefore, it cannot be referenced in EventsToRegister\n   - Even if declared in EventsToRegister, there's no handler case for it (second bug)\n   - Result: ResourceSlice events never reach the scheduler queue\n\n3. **The Fix Is Minimal**:\n   - Add one GVK constant (1 line)\n   - Add one switch case with 6-10 lines of code\n   - Add one optional queueing hint function (3-4 lines)\n   - Total: ~15 lines of code\n\n### Impact\n\n- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod\n- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads\n",

# Kubernetes Scheduler ResourceSlice Event Handler Bug Investigation

## Files Examined
- `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — Entry point for scheduling cycle
- `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` — Event handler registration mechanism for all cluster events
- `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` — GVK constants for all tracked resource types
- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` — DRA plugin implementation and EventsToRegister
- `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/informers/resource/v1alpha2/resourceslice.go` — ResourceSlice informer factory
- `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/structuredparameters.go` — Resource model building from ResourceSlices

## Dependency Chain

1. **Symptom observed in**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` (ScheduleOne function, line 66-134)
   - Pod scheduling occurs, fails with "cannot allocate all claims"
   - Pod is added to unschedulable queue
   - No re-evaluation happens when ResourceSlices are created

2. **Called from**: `pkg/scheduler/scheduler.go` (scheduler initialization)
   - Calls `addAllEventHandlers()` to register event handlers for resource changes

3. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` (addAllEventHandlers function, line 285-546)
   - Registers event handlers for multiple resource types via a gvkMap switch statement (lines 395-543)
   - **MISSING**: No case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in the switch statement
   - Covers: CSINode, CSIDriver, CSIStorageCapacity, PersistentVolume, PersistentVolumeClaim, PodSchedulingContext, ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, ResourceClaimParameters, ResourceClassParameters, StorageClass

4. **Framework issue in**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (GVK constants, lines 68-106)
   - **MISSING**: No `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined
   - Reso
... (truncated)
2. EDIT /logs/agent/solution.md
Before
### Impact

- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod
- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads
After
### Impact

- **Without Fix**: Pods requesting DRA devices are permanently stuck if the driver starts after the pod
- **With Fix**: Pods are automatically re-queued when ResourceSlices become available, enabling proper scheduling of DRA-dependent workloads

## Verification

### Code Pattern Confirmation
The fix follows the exact same pattern as other DRA resources:
- ResourceClaim handler (lines 457-465): Checks DynamicResourceAllocation feature gate, gets informer, adds event handler
- ResourceClass handler (lines 466-474): Same pattern
- **Proposed ResourceSlice handler**: Identical pattern, just with ResourceSlices() instead of ResourceClaims()

### Evidence That This Is The Bug
1. **Plugin uses ResourceSlices** (dynamicresources.go:958):
   - `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)` is called during Prefilter
   - Plugin queries ResourceSlices to determine available resources

2. **ResourceSlices are gettable** (scheduler initialization, line 356):
   - `fh.SharedInformerFactory().Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Lister()` shows ResourceSlices informer exists

3. **But no event handler is registered**:
   - No GVK constant for ResourceSlice
   - No case in eventhandlers.go switch statement
   - Therefore events are never delivered to the scheduling queue

4. **The fix is minimal** (15 lines total):
   - Only adds the missing integration points
   - Doesn't change any existing logic
   - Uses the exact same patterns as ResourceClaim, ResourceClass, etc.

## Summary

This is a **critical bug in the event-driven re-queuing mechanism** of the Kubernetes scheduler. When Dynamic Resource Allocation drivers publish ResourceSlice objects with available resources, the scheduler is never notified because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the schedul
